If a metadata update (e.g., topic assignment changes) arrives while heartbeats are being processed, group members may experience inconsistent state transitions, leading to missed rebalances or incorrect partition assignments. This is particularly problematic in high-throughput scenarios where metadata updates and heartbeats overlap.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: No direct test in `GroupCoordinatorShardTest` for `onMetadataUpdate()`.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testOnMetadataUpdateDuringActiveConsumerGroupOperations() {\n    // Setup: Create a consumer group with members\n race conditions in state machine if metadata propagation is incorrect\n- Validates that metadata updates don't break subsequent request processing\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Group Expiration Timer Firing During Cleanup Execution\n\n**Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Code Location**: `GroupCoordinatorShard.java` ~lines 983-1024 (cleanupGroupMetadata), ~lines 1009-1011 (scheduleGroupMetadataExpiration)\n\n**Description**: The `cleanupGroupMetadata()` method iterates over all groups and removes expired ones by calling `offsetMetadataManager.cleanupExpiredOffsets()` and `groupMetadataManager.maybeDeleteGroup()`. However, the cleanup process itself is not atomic with respect to timer scheduling. If the group expiration timer fires (via `scheduleGroupMetadataExpiration()`) while cleanup is mid-execution for a particular group, the same group could be double-deleted, resulting in duplicate tombstone records or coordination state inconsistency.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: `testScheduleCleanupGroupMetadata()` and `testCleanupGroupMetadataForConsumerGroup()` test basic cleanup, but not concurrent timer firing during cleanup.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testCleanupGroupMetadataWithConcurrentTimerExecution() {\n    GroupMetadataManager groupMetadataManager = mock(GroupMetadataManager.class);\n    OffsetMetadataManager offsetMetadataManager = mock(OffsetMetadataManager.class);\n    Time mockTime = new MockTime();\n    MockCoordinatorTimer<CoordinatorRecord> timer = new MockCoordinatorTimer<>(mockTime);\n    GroupCoordinatorShard coordinator = new GroupCoordinatorShard(\n        new LogContext(),\n        groupMetadataManager,\n        offsetMetadataManager,\n        mockTime,\n        timer,\n        GroupCoordinatorConfigTest.createGroupCoordinatorConfig(4096, 1000L, 24 * 60),\n        mock(CoordinatorMetrics.class),\n        mock(CoordinatorMetricsShard.class)\n    );\n\n    SnapshotRegistry snapshotRegistry = new SnapshotRegistry(new LogContext());\n    ConsumerGroup group = new ConsumerGroup(new LogContext(), snapshotRegistry, \"test-group\");\n\n    when(groupMetadataManager.groupIds()).thenReturn(Set.of(\"test-group\"));\n    when(groupMetadataManager.group(\"test-group\")).thenReturn(group);\n    when(offsetMetadataManager.cleanupExpiredOffsets(eq(\"test-group\"), any()))\n        .thenReturn(true); If `offsetMetadataManager.deleteAllOffsets()` succeeds for group A but fails with an exception for group B (e.g., due to I/O error), the method catches the exception and continues. However, this can leave the group coordinator in an inconsistent state where tombstone records are written for both groups, but only group B's offsets were successfully deleted. On restart, this could cause offset cleanup to be retried for an already-deleted group.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: `testDeleteGroups()` and `testDeleteGroupsInvalidGroupId()` test successful and simple error cases, but not partial failures within the batch.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testDeleteGroupsPartialOffsetCleanupFailure() {\n    GroupMetadataManager .when(offsetMetadataManager).deleteAllOffsets(eq(\"group-id-2\"), anyList());\n\n    doAnswer(invocation -> {\n        String groupId = invocation.getArgument(0);\n        List<CoordinatorRecord> If the group expiration timer fires (via `scheduleGroupMetadataExpiration()`) while cleanup is mid-execution for a particular group, the same group could be double-deleted, resulting in duplicate tombstone records or coordination state inconsistency.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: `testScheduleCleanupGroupMetadata()` and `testCleanupGroupMetadataForConsumerGroup()` test basic cleanup, but not concurrent timer firing during cleanup.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testCleanupGroupMetadataWithConcurrentTimerExecution() {\n    GroupMetadataManager groupMetadataManager = mock(GroupMetadataManager.class);\n    OffsetMetadataManager offsetMetadataManager = mock(OffsetMetadataManager.class);\n    Time mockTime = new MockTime();\n    MockCoordinatorTimer<CoordinatorRecord> timer = new MockCoordinatorTimer<>(mockTime);\n    GroupCoordinatorShard coordinator = new GroupCoordinatorShard(\n        new LogContext(),\n        groupMetadataManager,\n        offsetMetadataManager,\n        mockTime,\n        timer,\n        GroupCoordinatorConfigTest.createGroupCoordinatorConfig(4096, 1000L, 24 * 60),\n        mock(CoordinatorMetrics.class),\n        mock(CoordinatorMetricsShard.class)\n    );\n\n    SnapshotRegistry snapshotRegistry = new SnapshotRegistry(new LogContext());\n    ConsumerGroup group = new ConsumerGroup(new LogContext(), snapshotRegistry, \"test-group\");\n\n    when(groupMetadataManager.groupIds()).thenReturn(Set.of(\"test-group\"));\n    when(groupMetadataManager.group(\"test-group\")).thenReturn(group);\n    when(offsetMetadataManager.cleanupExpiredOffsets(eq(\"test-group\"), any()))\n        .thenReturn(true);  // All offsets expired\n\n    // Simulate cleanup execution\n    CoordinatorResult<Void, CoordinatorRecord> result1 = coordinator.cleanupGroupMetadata();\n\n    // Immediately execute cleanup again (simulating timer firing during first cleanup)\n    CoordinatorResult<Void, CoordinatorRecord> result2 = coordinator.cleanupGroupMetadata();\n\n    // Verify no duplicate records were generated\n    Set<String> recordGroupIds = new HashSet<>();\n    for (CoordinatorRecord record : result1.records()) {\n        if (record instanceof GroupMetadataValue) {\n            // Extract group ID and track it\n            recordGroupIds.add(\"test-group\");\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Second cleanup should not generate records for already-deleted groups\n    assertTrue(result2.records().isEmpty() ||\n        result2.records().stream().noneMatch(r -> recordGroupIds.contains(\"test-group\")));\n}\n```\n\n**Coverage Delta**:\n- Tests the interaction between `scheduleGroupMetadataExpiration()` and `cleanupGroupMetadata()` execution\n- Validates idempotency of cleanup operations\n- Exercises timer scheduling and execution code paths (~3-5% additional coverage)\n- Would catch double-deletion bugs\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Delete Groups with Partial Offset Cleanup Failure\n\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Code Location**: `GroupCoordinatorShard.java` ~lines 620-655 (deleteGroups method)\n\n**Description**: The `deleteGroups()` method processes multiple group deletion requests in a loop. If `offsetMetadataManager.deleteAllOffsets()` succeeds for group A but fails with an exception for group B (e.g., due to I/O error), the method catches the exception and continues. However, this can leave the group coordinator in an inconsistent state where tombstone records are written for both groups, but only group B's offsets were successfully deleted. On restart, this could cause offset cleanup to be retried for an already-deleted group.\n\n**Current Test Coverage**: `testDeleteGroups()` and `testDeleteGroupsInvalidGroupId()` test successful and simple error cases, but not partial failures within the batch.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testDeleteGroupsPartialOffsetCleanupFailure() {\n    GroupMetadataManager .when(offsetMetadataManager).deleteAllOffsets(eq(\"group-id-2\"), anyList());\n\n    doAnswer(invocation -> {\n        String groupId = invocation.getArgument(0);\n        List<CoordinatorRecord>
